text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">pÅ¡/- </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">(ab¥q p¡q¡)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span></span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">Ef f¢lQ¡mL</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">hÉ¡w¢Lw fË¢h¢d J e£¢a ¢hi¡N z </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">¯^vt/-<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span></span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">(®j¡x CLh¡m ®q¡­</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">‡</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">pe)</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">Ef-f¢lQ¡mL z</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">hÉ¡w¢Lw fË¢h¢d<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>J e£¢a ¢hi¡Nz</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(emphasis added)</span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">What action Bangladesh Bank or the Finance Division of the Ministry of Finance has taken, on the basis of this recommendation or what is/are the subsequent developments (if there were any) have not been placed before this Court. Nor this Court is informed whether any action, as per the recommendation quoted above, has at all been taken or not. </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Be that as it may, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benami</em> <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">shares</em> (i.e. the shares held in the name of other persons) in the banking company is not legally permissible in as much as that will render ineffective the restrictions imposed under sub-section (1) of section ‘14Ka’ of the Banking Companies Act, 1991 (BCA) as regards the maximum limit of shares that a person can hold in a banking company and that will render the intent and purport of section ‘14Ka’ a total nullity. Whereas, sub-section (2) of section ‘14Ka’ of the BCA, that has made the intent more clear, reads as follows:</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">(2) ®L¡e hÉ¡wL ®L¡Çf¡e£ LaÑªL k¡¢Qa qC­m EJ² hÉ¡w­Ll ®nu¡l H²­ul pju ®H²a¡ HC j­jÑ nfbfœ h¡ ®O¡oe¡fœ c¡¢Mm L¢l­he ®k, ¢a¢e A­eÉl j­e¡e£a hÉ¡¢J² ¢qp¡­h h¡ ®he¡j£­a ®nu¡l H²u L¢l­a­Re e¡ Hhw C¢af§­hÑ ®he¡j£­a ®L¡e ®nu¡l H²u L­le e¡Cz </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The clear intent and purport of law is not to allow holding any <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benemi </em>share in any bank, scheduled as well as non-scheduled. Therefore, the persons (if any) who are holding 85,000 or any number of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benami shares</em> shall not be entitled to attend in the aforesaid AGMs, since, Court should not allow anybody to indirectly exceeded the limit fixed by section ‘14Ka’ of the Bank Companies Act, 1991, to secure unlawful advantage by frustrating the law or by committing fraud on statute.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Therefore, the RJSC should be directed to hold an inspection in respect of all relevant records lying with it and the share register of the said bank and shall submit a report to the Independent Chairman alongwith a list of shareholders (members), separately showing the ‘<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benami shares</em>’ and name of the ‘<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benami shareholders’</em>(as reported). Notice of any AGM of the bank shall not be sent to the ‘<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benami shareholders’</em> (as per list of RJSC), but to all other shareholders.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Bangladesh Bank may, as per the report quoted above, forfeit the shares of Mr. M.B.I. Munshi and of any other person, who is /are holding shares, in the said bank, in excess of the statutory maximum fixed by section ‘14Ka’of the Bank Companies Act, 1991, subject to the amendment (if any) and only after issuing a notice upon the persons concerned, asking him/them to show cause as to why the said excess shares (as reported) shall not be forfeited and sold or as to why the title in those shares shall not be vested in the Government.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The newly elected board shall nominate 3(three) competent persons as Managing Director of Jubilee Bank Limited and shall send the name to Bangladesh Bank for their approval within 30(thirty) days of the first meeting of the newly elected board of directors. Bangladesh Bank may also appoint an “Observer” for the Jubilee Bank Limited.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Bangladesh Bank, as soon as possible, but not exceeding 30(thirty) days of drawing up of this judgment and order, shall decide, having regard to the authority vested in it under sections 45, 46 and 47 of the Bank Companies Act, 1991 (BCA), if the present board of directors shall continue to function till holding of the outstanding AGMs or if the existing Board should be dissolved or any director should be removed.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Bangladesh Bank shall also ascertain and give direction, as permitted by section 45(1) of the Bank Companies Act, 1991, if a fresh balance sheet, profit and loss account, board report, and audit report for holding the 96<sup>th</sup> to 101<sup>st</sup> AGM will be required or not.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">As regards the objection raised about the locus-standi of the petitioner, I am of the opinion that, this is not a petition under section 43 of the Act. Rather as per provisions of sub-section (3) of section 85, this Court can suo-moto pass an order for holding all these AGM afresh. Hence, the question of locus-standi of the petitioner is not relevant, nor required to be decided in passing any judgment and order under section 85(3) of the Companies Act, 1994. </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The persons already found guilty for committing contempt of Court is hereby declared disqualified to be candidate in 96<sup>th</sup> to 103<sup>rd</sup> AGMs, since they have committed gross violation of their statutory and fiduciary duties and should not be placed in the position of trust in or agent for the bank. Similarly, if it is proved before the independent Chairman that, the petitioner is a shareholder, then only he can participate in the AGM/election, not otherwise. The AGMs should be held within 60 (sixty) days of submitting list of members by the RJSC to the independent Chairman.</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">R D E R:</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">In the result the application is allowed with the following direction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(1)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The 96<sup>th</sup> to 101<sup>st</sup> AGM are hereby declared not to have been held properly, or as per law, hence minutes of the said AGMs and all notices (if issued), the returns and the balance sheet filed with the RJSC shall stand cancelled.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(2)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The entire period of delay that has occurred in holding the 96<sup>th</sup> to 101<sup>st </sup>AGMs for the calendar years 2009, 2010, 2011, 2012, 2013, and 2014, is hereby condoned. Since, in the meantime the AGMs for the subsequent years have also been delayed, therefore, the delay in respect of the AGMs due for the years 2015, 2016 and 2017 is hereby condoned as well.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(3)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Since, there is a dispute admitted by the parties in respect of share holding position as well as ‘<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benamai shares</em>, therefore, the respondent No. 9 RJSC is directed to hold an inspection of the records of the said company, either by himself or through other competent officials/team of the said office. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(4)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In the light of the inspection result, the RJSC shall prepare an upto date list of shareholders (having original share certificates), separately showing name of those shareholders who are holding shares in their own name and the holders of the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">benami</em> shares (if any) and shall also address such other issues as may be required to arrive at a proper decision upon consideration of proper and relevant materials and they should submit their report within 3(three) months of receiving this judgment and order.</span></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--></span><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/January__2019(1)/Issue%20__January__19__Company__315%20of%2017_Md.%20Rezaul%20Hasan,%20J.__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Company Matter No. 315 of 2017</span></strong></a></span></p></div></div></div></div>
715	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Mofazzel Gazi and others  Vs.  Abdul Hamid Gazi and others, (Soumendra Sarker, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 203(con) of 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mahbub-Ule-Islam, Advocate with Mr. Md. Mahibullah Tanvir, Advocate, Mr. Sharder Abul Hossain, Advocate with Mrs. Tahmina Akhter, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Mofazzel Gazi @ Md. Mofazzel Hossain and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Abdul Hamid Gazi and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Limitation Act  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-26</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><span style="font-size: 13.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: AR-SA;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Soumendra Sarker, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">01.02.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/January__2019(1)/Issue%20__January__19__C.%20R.%20203%20of%2017_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mofazzel Gazi @ Md. Mofazzel Hossain and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . .Petitioner-Applicant</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Abdul Hamid Gazi and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . .Plaintiff-Opposite party.</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Limitation Act (IX of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 5</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The limitation can be condoned, and only where it is found that the delay caused was not for the negligence of the party concerned and when it is found that the cause of delay is reasonable, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> and sufficient, in that case only the delay occurred can be condoned.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Each day of delay is required be explained from the date of expiry of limitation, up to the date of institution of the case. Negligence, even ignorance of law is not a sufficient ground within the meaning of this section and “sufficient cause” means something beyond the control of the party. The law of limitation or section 05 there under cannot help a dormant like the present applicants. Besides, the inordinate delay which is 1,176 days, is not properly explained at all from the side of the petitioners in their application for condonation of delay. . . . (10, 11 and 12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Mahbub-Ule-Islam, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Mahibullah Tanvir, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the petitioner</span></em></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">s</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Mr. Sharder Abul Hossain, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mrs. Tahmina Akhter, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the opposite parties.</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Soumendra Sarker, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule issued calling upon the Opposite parties No. 1(a)-1(i) and 2-6 to show cause as to why the delay of 1176 days in preferring the Civil Revision should not be condoned and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts leading to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated thus, the present applicants as petitioners filed an application for revision under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure after the expiry of 1176 days which was the delay in filing the revision application. The petitioners were the defendants to the Original Title Suit being No. 34 of 1993, which was decreed in the preliminary form by the trial court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved the defendants to that suit preferred a Title Appeal being No. 244 of 2006 in the court of the learned District Judge, Khulna which was allowed in part, modifying <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the judgment and decree passed by the trial court</span> by the judgment and decree dated 08.10.2013. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and decree the defendant-petitioners preferred the Civil Revision before this court which was 1176 days time barred. For condonation of the said delay the petitioner-applicants have filed this application under section 05 of the Limitation Act and obtained the Rule with an interim order of stay. The grounds cited in the contents of this application for condonation of delay in a nutshell is such, that the impugned judgment and decree was passed by the learned appellate court on 08.10.2013 and the decree was singed on 20.10.2013 and the learned Advocate who <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">was engaged on behalf of the petitioners, for the</span> reason best known to him, did not communicate the petitioners about the impugned judgment and decree. The further case of the petitioners is such that a learned Advocate Commissioner who was appointed in connection of that decree, without service any notices upon the petitioners and without taking any measurement, filed his report, pursuant to which the opposite parties have obtained a final decree on 28.09.2016 and filed an Execution Case being No. 09 of 2016, but on 05.02.2017 the petitioners were informed about the judgment and decree and the Execution Case through the clerk of the engaged Advocate. Thereafter the petitioner-applicants filed an application for certified copy on 06.02.2017 which was delivered on 23.02.2017. It was the further case of the petitioners that, knowing about the judgment and decree they have communicated with their engaged lawyer who advised them to collect the certified copy of the judgment and decree. After receiving the certified copy, the petitioners went to the chamber of their lawyer who preferred the revisional application and in this way there has been delay of 1176 days and for that reason the petitioners prays for condonation of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>delay. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">During hearing of the Rule Mr.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Mahbub</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">-Ule-Islam, the learned Advocate along with Mr. Mahibullah Tanvir, the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the petitioner-applicants while Mr. Sharder Abul Hossain, and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Mrs. Tahmina Akhter, the learned Advocates appeared on behalf of the opposite parties. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocates appearing on behalf of the petitioners submits that the delay occurred in filing the revisional application was beyond the control of the petitioners and the petitioners were in the dark about the judgment and decree passed by the appellate court and the Execution Case being No. 09 of 2016. The learned Advocate further submits that for the reason described in paragraph No. 02 of the application for condonation of delay, the delay of 1176 days occurred which was <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> and reasonable. The learned Advocates lastly submits that the petitioner-applicants have got a good case on merit and there is a fair chance of success from their side in the Civil Revision. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">As against the aforesaid submission of the learned Advocates for the petitioners, the learned Advocates appearing on behalf of the opposite parties opposing the Rule submits that, the petitioners were very much aware of the judgment and decree passed by the learned appellate court in Title Appeal No. 244 of 2006 and in their presence the decree was passed. The learned Advocate further submits that knowing fully well about the judgment and decree passed by the learned appellate court, the petitioner-applicants remained dormant and <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">after a long laps of 1176 days, on false allegation</span> they have filed the application for condonation of delay, which is not <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> and there is no sufficient cause from their side for condonation <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">of delay under Section 05 of the Limitation Act.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Considering the submission of the learned Advocates, having gone through the application for condonation of delay it transpires that, the reason cited from the side of the applicants for their delay is such, that they were in the dark about the judgment and decree passed by the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>appellate court in Title Appeal No. 244 of 2006 since their engaged lawyer did not communicate the result of the appeal to them and for the 1<sup>st</sup> time, when the Execution Case being No. 09 of 2016 was started<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>on the basis of final decree dated 28.09.2016, the clerk of the engaged lawyer informed them about the judgment and decree on 05.02.2017 and thereafter taking advice from their engaged <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">lawyer they filed an application for getting certified</span> copy of the judgment and decree on 06.02.2017 and obtained the same on 23.02.2017.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Consulting the relevant papers I find that the Title Appeal being No. 244 of 2006 was filed by the present-petitioners and the learned appellate court after hearing from both the sides passed the impugned judgment and decree on 08.10.2013. It further appears from the connected papers that the learned lawyer who was engaged on behalf of the petitioners was one<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Mr. Abdul Hamid Gazi and it appears from the application for condonation of delay that the petitioners knowing about the judgment and decree communicated with Mr. Mahabubul Islam, the learned Advocate who allegedly advised them to collect the certified copy of the judgment and decree. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is to be remembered that, under Section 05 of the Limitation Act, 1908 in some special cases, the limitation can be condoned, and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>only where it is found that the delay caused was not for the negligence of the party concerned and when it is found that the cause of delay is reasonable, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> and sufficient, in that case only the delay occurred can be condoned. In the case of Abul Hossen vs. State 1 BLC (AD) 40, our Apex court held that in absence of any sufficient cause for condonation of delay the inordinate delay can not be condoned. This bench also in the case of Ms. Ok-Kyung Oh vs. Tea Hung Packaging (BD) Ltd. and Others 24 BLT (HCD) 240 held that, the negligent conduct, self-styled assumption of certain facts, ignorance of law or misapplication of law cannot form valid basis for condonation of delay. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Apart from this, it is a decided matter in our judicature that each day of delay is required be explained from the date of expiry of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>limitation, up to the date of institution of the case. Negligence, even ignorance of law is not a sufficient ground within the meaning of this section and “sufficient cause” means something beyond the control of the party. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant case, as I have come across from the facts and circumstances of the case that the reason of delay cited in the application for condonation of delay is in no way can be treated as <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> or sufficient cause, inasmuch as; it is the petitioner-applicants who filed the Title Appeal being No. 244 of 2006 which was disposed of in their presence by the learned appellate court on 08.10.2013. The law of limitation or section 05 there under cannot help a dormant like the present applicants. Besides, the inordinate delay which is 1,176 days, is not properly explained at all from the side of the petitioners in their application for condonation of delay. </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/January__2019(1)/Issue%20__January__19__C.%20R.%20203%20of%2017_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">203(con) of 2017</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
716	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Most. Rabeya Khatoon Vs. Jahanara @ Shefali Bewa, (Nazmun Ara Sultana, J.) </h2>

Nizamul Huq J</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Md. Taufique Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ (AD) </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Most. Rabeya Khatoon being dead her heirs: Md. Abdur Rakib Sarker and others </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Jahanara alias Shefali Bewa being dead her heirs: Salma Akter alias Most. Maya Khatun and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Mahomedan Law </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-26</p><!DOCTYPE html><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"> </p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 104.9pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top" width="140"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md.
