mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">07.12.2016</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 16.1pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/January__2019(1)/Issue__January_19__C.%20A.%20324%20of%2009__Mirza%20Hussain%20Haider_J___AD___1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 93.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Pranay Kumar Malakar and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Appellants</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Chowdhury Makhlisur Rahman </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">...Respondent</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Sections 45 and 73</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">When modern technologies are available in comparing the disputed signatures with the admitted signature the court should not take the risk of comparing the signature by itself when the experts with modern technologies are available.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                           </span>. . . (18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Sections 45 and 73</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In respect of thumb impression it is not at all </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">possible to justify whether one thumb impression</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> matches with other by naked eye other than with the help of modern technique and enlargement of impression for which the Expert is the right person who can give opinion upon critical analyses of all marks of the impressions. . . . (18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Specific Relief Act (I of 1877) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 12</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In a suit for specific performance of Contract the plaintiff is to prove that there was a talk of sale, pursuant to the said talk consideration/earnest money was passed and an agreement for sale(bainapatra) was executed by the vendor stipulating certain conditions, if any, to enforce the agreement. In the present case the plaintiff respondent failed to prove all the above conditions including those of the signatures and thumb impressions in the bainapatra.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . (19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the<span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> Appellants</span> :</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Mr. Abdul Wadud</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Bhuiyan, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Mvi. Md. <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Wahidullah, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Respondent</span> :</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Chowdhury Md. Zahangir, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J.</span></u></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN;">:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> This civil appeal, by leave, is directed against judgment and decree dated 18.04.2006 passed by a Single Bench of the High Court Division in Civil Revision No. 3652 of 2001 making the Rule absolute upon setting aside the judgment and decree dated 25.05.2000 passed by the learned Additional District Judge, Moulavibazar, in Title Appeal No. 134 of 1996 and thereby affirming the judgment and decree 22.09.1996, passed by the learned Subordinate Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Moulavibazar, in Title Suit No. 10 of 1990 decreeing the suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Facts, leading to filing of this appeal, in<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>a nutshell, are: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">That the present respondent No.1 as plaintiff, instituted Title Suit No. 244 of 1980 in the Court of the then Subordinate Judge,(now Joint District Judge), 2<sup>nd</sup> Court, Sylhet, impleading the present appellant as defendant for specific performance of contract. The said suit was decreed on 19.02.1982. Thereafter, the defendant appellants preferred appeal before the learned District Judge, Sylhet which was subsequently re-numbered as Title Appeal No. 81 of 1985 in the Court of learned District Judge, Moulavibazar, after Moulavibazar District Judgeship was created.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The learned District Judge, Moulavibazar after hearing the same allowed the appeal by his judgment and decree dated 19.02.1982 and sent back the suit on remand with observation that the signature of the defendant No.1 and left thumb impression of the defendant No.2 be examined by experts and the parties to adduce evidence if they so like. After remand the plaintiff got the signature and left thumb impression of defendant Nos. 1 and 2, respectively, examined by the CID of Police and the suit was transferred to the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of learned Subordinate Judge(now Joint District Judge) Moulavibazar being re numbered as Title Suit No. 10 of 1990. After hearing the trial Court decreed the suit by judgment and decree dated 02.02.1996, which was reversed in appeal by the judgment and decree dated 25.05.2000 passed by the learned Additional District Judge, Moulavibazar in Title Appeal No. 134 of 1996. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The case of the plaintiff, in short, is that, defendants No. 1 and 2, along with their other co-sharers being owners of the suit land as well as other lands agreed to sell their land to the plaintiff at a consideration of TK.60,000/- and the value of the share of the defendants No. 1 and 2 was fixed at TK.20,000/= as the co-owner of </span><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(1,3) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">rd of the suit land. As per the agreement other co-sharers on receipt of TK.40,000/= transferred their </span><!-- [if supportFields]><span lang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(2,3) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">rd shares to the plaintiff by executing registered kabala. The defendant Nos. 1 and 2 on receipt of TK.15,000/= out of the agreed amount of TK.20,000/= executed a deed of agreement (Bainapatra) on 01.04.1980 in favour of the plaintiff in respect of their </span><!-- [if supportFields]><span lang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(1,3) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">rd share stipulating that on receipt of the rest of the amount of consideration within next three months they would execute and register the kabala. But subsequently they denied executing and registering the kabala lastly on 30.06.1980 when the plaintiff demanded for the same. Hence the suit. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The defendant Nos. 1 and 2 contested the suit by filing written statement denying the claim of the plaintiff contending, inter alia, that they did not execute any bainapatra nor did they receive any amount as earnest money from the plaintiff. The plaintiff with an intention to grab the suit land, in collusion with the scribe and the attesting witnesses, created a forged<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>bainapatra and instituted the suit.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>That in respect of the said land along with other lands they filed Partition Suit No. 102 of 1980 wherein by an order dated 10.05.1980 the defendants of that suit were asked to show cause as to why they would not be restrained by an order of injunction from transferring the suit land to others. The deed of transfer dated 24.05.1980 as mentioned in the plaint was executed after issuance of the aforesaid show cause notice. They claimed that Jogendra Ram Malakar was the owner of </span><!-- [if supportFields]><span lang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(1,3) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">rd share of the disputed homestead and his share became enemy property. That on 14.05.1980 the plaintiff filed an application to the authority to take lease of that </span><!-- [if supportFields]><span lang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(1,3) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">rd share left behind by Jogendra Ram Malakar but on an application filed by them (defendants) the Deputy Commissioner stayed all further proceedings in respect of that enemy property and hence the suit was liable to be dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The trial Court on hearing the parties decreed Title Suit No. 10 of 1990 by judgment and decree dated 22.09.1996. The said decree was challenged by the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Defendants-appellants in Title Appeal No.134 of 1996. On hearing the learned Additional District Judge, Moulvibazar, by judgment and decree dated 25.5.2000 allowed the same and set aside the judgment and decree of the trial court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Being aggrieved by the said judgment and decree of the appellate court the plaintiff-respondent filed civil Revision No.3652 of 2001 before the High Court Division and obtained Rule which was ultimately made absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Hence, the defendant appellants filed civil petition for Leave to Appeal No. 272 of 2008 and obtained leave giving rise to the instant Civil Appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. M Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan, the learned Senior Counsel appearing on behalf of the appellants submits that the law permits the court to compare signature of a person with his admitted signatures yet in respect of comparison of thumb impression or signature the court usually instead of doing it by itself may take assistance of an expert having knowledge of developed scientific process and method of examination in this respect. It is hazardous and risky for the Court even the High Court Division<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>itself to sit as an expert in order to examine and scrutinize the signature and thumb impression on the impugned Bainapatra for ascertaining similarity and dissimilarity of signature or thumb impression when there is already an expert report in the case and therefore, the High Court Division committed<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>an error of law in setting<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>aside the judgment of the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>court of appeal below and, as such, considering the same the impugned judgment and order passed by the High Court Division is liable to be set<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>aside. He next submits that the plaintiff failed to prove purchase of the stamp paper which has been used in the alleged bainapatra which is apparent on the face of it appears to have been purchased four months back and in the name of one Abdur Rahman, who is not a party in the said bainapatra. He finally submits that the suit land is the only paternal homestead belonging to the defendant-appellants and if the decree or specific performance of contract is enforced, they are to go to the street leaving their only paternal homestead and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in such consideration of the matter the High Court Division ought not to have exercised its discretion in granting specific performance of contract. Considering the facts and circumstances the impugned judgment and order passed by the High Court Division is liable to be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Mahabubey Alam, the learned Senior Counsel appearing on behalf of the plaintiff-respondent, submits that the plaintiff respondent by adducing adequate evidences has been able to prove the signature of the defendants in the Bainapatra which the trail court as well as the High Court Division, upon proper scrutinisation found it to be of the defendants and as such decreed the suit which does not call for any interference by this Division. Thus the instant civil appeal may kingly be dismissed. He finally submits that the defendant- appellants in their pleadings having not made any statement that if the decree for specific performance of contract is enforced they are to go to the street leaving their only paternal homestead and in that view the instant appeal is liable to be dismissed</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We have considered the submissions of the learned senior advocates of both the sides and perused the impugned judgment of the High Court Division and other materials on record. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The moot question in this case is whether the signatures and thumb impression on the bainapatra was<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>genuine and whether it was risky/hazardous for the High Court Division itself to sit as an expert in order to examine and scrutinize the signature and thumb impression on the impugned bainapatra for ascertainment of similarity and dissimilarity of signature or thumb impression wherein there is already an expert report in the case. The trial Court on the face of specific denial of the defendants and direction of the appellate court below sent the signatures and thumb impression of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>defendants No. 1 and 2 to the Handwriting Expert for examination and report on comparing the same with their admitted signatures. The Handwriting Expert of CID, Police, examined the same and sent his report which the trial Court did not accept; rather it examined the signatures and the thumb impression of its own and considering other materials on record decreed the suit.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The Court of appeal below, on the other hand, on consideration of all the materials on record, having found discrepancy in the signature and thumb impression of the defendants and also in respect of purchasing stamp papers used in bainapatra, absence of the father in law of the plaintiff at the time of writing of the bainapatra and also found that the plaintiff has failed to prove that the consideration money was passed by producing sufficient evidence, allowed the appeal and dismissed the suit.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The Court of appeal below in respect of discarding the opinion of the Handwriting Expert relating to signatures and thumb impression, observed that ‘no doubt a Court can itself compare the writings in order to appreciate properly the other evidences produced before it in that regard. But the opinion of Handwriting Expert is also relevant in view of section 45 of the Evidence Act, but that too is not conclusive’. The Court of appeal below relying on the principle that ‘task of arriving at a sound opinion is always fraught with difficulties’ and, as such, a Court for the reasons as aforesaid either shall have to abandon the duty or reject the opinion of a qualified expert merely because his evidence is an opinion evidence. In the absence of better evidence opinion evidence has to be utilized by course of law in respect of forming opinion’.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Thus considering the fact that the trial court did not accepted the opinion of expert and rather disregarded the same. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Court of appeal below under such circumstances considered all the evidence, both oral and documentary on record and found that the plaintiff as P.W. 1 in his cross examination stated that “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Avgvi evqbvgv cÎ mZ¨ weavq Avwg</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Expert examination </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-ansi-language: EN;">KivBe bv GÛ Bnv mZ¨ b‡n evqbv cÎ</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Expert examination </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-ansi-language: EN;">KivB‡j Rvj cÖgvwYZ nB‡e weavq Dnv</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> expert </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-ansi-language: EN;">×viv</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> examination </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Kivq bvB|</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">” and came to a conclusion that the motive of P.W. 1 is very clear. Again in respect of purchasing stamp paper and writings of bainapatra and passing of consideration money the court of appeal below upon considering all evidences on record held that the trial Court was wrong in coming to the conclusion that the suit should be decreed on misconception of law and misinterpretation of evidence and thus allowed the appeal and thereby dismissing the suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Apart from the above on consideration of the deposition of PW 1 it appears that he stated that the bainapatra was executed in his shop when his father-in-law<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>who claimed to have negotiated the transfer was not present; At 11.00 am he brought the scribe from the Court;<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>he did not inform the witness or the scribe earlier that on the said date bainapatra would be written. He went to the court and purchased the stamp paper and he took the scribe to his shop when he kept the defendants No. 1 and 2 sitting at Rokman Ali’s shop. But the scribe Abdul Matin<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>(PW-6) on the other hand deposed that ‘he was informed at 11.30 am by the plaintiff at the Registry Office that he<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>would have to write the bainapatra. Plaintiff purchased one stamp paper on that particular date and took it to his shop’. On the other hand on scrutinizing the bainapatra (Exhibit-2) which is shown to have been executed on 18<sup>th</sup> Chatra 1386 BS<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>corresponding to 01.04.1980 it appears that the same was purchased in the name of one Abdur Rahman of Sylhet,(who is not a party to the same) on 02.01.1980 corresponding to 17<sup>th</sup> Poush 1386 BS approximately four months before the alleged date of execution of the said bainapatra. Relying on such evidence the appellate court held that neither the plaintiff nor the defendants purchased the stamp paper for the purpose of the said bainapatra.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>As such the plaintiff dismantled and dislodged the genuineness and sanctity of execution of the bainapatra. Again from the evidence on record it appears that the father-in-law of the plaintiff, who was the negotiator of the sale, was not present at the time of transaction as well as writing of the bainapatra as admitted by the plaintiff himself. If the father-in-law of the plaintiff was the negotiator then there was no reason for the said negotiator to be not present at the time of writing of the bainapatra and be a witness of the said bainapatra instead of a shop keeper and a stranger to become attesting witnesses in the said bainapatra. Thus the Court of appeal below raised suspicion as to genuineness of the bainapatra. It further appears that the defendants being inhabitants of Kulaura under Moulvibazar District it is not understood as to why they would go to the station road in Sylhet<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to pay the earnest money on 01.04.1980 when the contract was made and execute the bainapatra on 02.01.1980 on a stamp paper purchased four months earlier in the name of a third party. Moreover there is no reason as to why the plaintiff shall pay the earnest money of TK.15,000/= out of TK.20,000/= when he got the sale deed registered from the other co sharers of the defendants No. 1 and 2 within<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>a week from the date of registration of the sale deed executed by other co sharers and why three years’ time would be given to pay the balance amount of only TK.5,000/= to the plaintiff.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On consideration of all the materials on record and the facts and circumstances stated above Court of appeal below observed that the aforesaid actions of the plaintiff itself proves forgery and fabrication in making the alleged bainapatra in collusion with the scribe and other attesting witnesses who are inhabitants of Sylhet whereas the property is situated at Kolaura under Moulvibazar District’. Moreover<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the conduct of the plaintiff and his father-in-law Mahbubuddin Chowdhury, admittedly a neighbor of the defendants,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>clearly show that they had been trying to grab the defendants’ </span><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(1,3) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanlang=EN style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-ansi-language:EN'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">rd share for which the defendants No. 1 and 2<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>earlier filed a suit and obtained temporary injunction against the plaintiff and other co sharers in the suit jote from transferring the same. Being unsuccessful to get the same the plaintiff in collusion with his father-in-law and others created the bainapatra by false personation showing the defendants No. 1 and 2 as the vendors. The plaintiff as PW-1 admitted about the filing of the said suit by the defendants in the court of Moulvibazar and also admitted about passing of the order of injunction against them. Thus the Court of appeal below allowed the appeal and dismissed the suit observing that the trial court was not justified in decreeing the suit which is based on misreading and misinterpretation of the evidence on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">From the impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division it appears that all the abovenoted findings of the lower appellate Court have not been met by the High Court Division while passing the impugned judgment. The High Court Division, it appears, relied upon the findings of the trial Court as well as itself considered and compared the same in respect of the comparison of the signature of the defendants No. 1 and 2 in the bainapatra and other documents and came to the finding that the signature in the bainapatra is genuine. In respect of the Handwriting Expert’s report the High Court Division observed “ the Handwriting Expert also stated in his report that <em>apparently the signatures in all the relevant papers<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>including the deed of agreement are of same hand but on further analyses the expert find some difference in respect of pen movement, density of ink or hesitation in putting the signature in the deed of agreement.”</em><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The High Court Division observed ‘since the trial Court did not consider the expert’s report as a correct one it compared<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the signature by itself and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>came to the conclusion that the signatures in all relevant papers are of same hand’. Thus it affirmed the said finding of the trial Court holding that there may be<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>some differences in the signature of one person to another because of time, age, health condition and mental condition of a person and, as such, the trial Court rightly discouraged such report’.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In respect of thumb impression the High Court Division observed that “it is further apparent that the thumb impressions are of same hand in respect of size and nature but there is some difference in respect of density of ink about such difference. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On these backdrops the Handwriting Expert report dated 08.07.1993 has been placed before us by filing additional paper book dated 28.11.2016.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Having gone through the same it appears that the High Court Division completely misread the same and without considering the entire report came to a wrong conclusion that the expert found that the signatures are of same hand. We have meticulously gone through the report which clearly shows that on comparison of the signature contained in the bainapatra along with other signature given in the vokalatnama and the admitted signature obtained on 25.5.2981 the expert found that the signature in the vokalatnama matches with the admitted signature of Pranay Kumar Malakar but none of those signatures matches with the signature which appears in the bainapatra. The expert at the concluding portion of his report opined as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-ansi-language: EN;">......D‡jøwLZ cv_©K¨¸wj †gŠwjK cÖK…wZi | ...... mvwe©K we‡ePbvq Avwg GB wm×v‡Í DcwbZ nBjvg †h, LÓ wmwiR wPwýZ cÖvgY¨ MÕ wmwiR wPwýZ bgybv ¯^v¶iMywji m¤úv`b Kvix<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>K, K-1 wPwýZ weZwK©Z ¯^v¶i `yBwU m¤úv`b K‡ib bvB | KÕ, K-1 wPwýZ ¯^v¶i `yBwU Bwg‡Ukb c×wZ‡Z Rvj ¯^v¶i |</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Similar was the finding in respect of thumb impression. So, on the face of such report by the Handwriting Expert the High Court Division committed serious error in relying on the opinion of the trial Court and also upon its one opinion and thereby erroneously passed the impugned judgment and order. No doubt the court is the expert of all experts as decided in the case of Abtab Ali(Captain, Retired) Vs. SM Kutubuddin (56 DLR(AD)117). But when modern technologies are available in comparing the disputed signatures with the admitted signature the court should not take the risk of comparing the signature by itself when the experts with modern technologies are available. This view finds support in the case of Serajuddin Ahmed (Md) and others Vs. AKM Saiful Alam and others (9 MLR (AD) 201) and Tarek Chandra Majhi Vs. Atahar Ali Hawlader and others (8 MLR (AD)209). In respect of thumb impression it is not at all possible to justify whether one thumb impression matches with other by naked eye other than with the help of modern technique and enlargement of impression for which the Expert is the right person who can give opinion upon critical analyses of all marks of the impressions, as decided in the cases cited above.  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">19.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In a suit for specific performance of Contract the plaintiff is to prove that there was a talk of sale, pursuant to the said talk consideration/earnest money was passed and an agreement for sale(bainapatra) was executed by the vendor stipulating certain conditions, if any, to enforce the agreement. In the present case <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">the plaintiff respondent failed to prove all the above</span> conditions including those of the signatures and thumb impressions in the bainapatra.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">20.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the reasons stated hereinabove we are of the view that the High Court Division was not at all justified in discarding the handwriting expert’s report and relying on the opinion of the trial Court and also examining the signature and thumb impression by itself and thereby it came to an erroneous decision which is liable to be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">21.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Accordingly, this civil appeal is allowed and the judgment and order complained of herein is set aside. There will be no order as to costs.  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Ed. </span></strong></p></div><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/January__2019(1)/Issue__January_19__C.%20A.%20324%20of%2009__Mirza%20Hussain%20Haider_J___AD___1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">CIVIL APPEAL </span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">No. 324 OF 2009.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(From the judgment and decree dated 18.04.2006 passed by the High Court Division in <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Civil Revision No. 3652 of 2001</span>).</span></p></div></div></div></div>
